  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_bcfdeef8-4f03-4975-b7aa-1669806bc55c'
      });
    }

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1868434239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11359429676403720351"> <b> Artemis </b> Always Has a Plan B!!!!!<br/><br/>This story is about a robbery of a diamond. Artemis teams up with Mulch, dwarf who is also a thief, for the robbery. <br/><br/>Well, this was really short. I didn't see any point in the story that could relate to the series. I am not saying it was a waste-of-time read. But I thought it was the part of this series. <br/>Anyways, it was a good read for me.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15385625287050239944">Okay Artemis Fowl fans, this is a SHORT STORY!! And by SHORT I mean short! It totals 59 pages!!- that's it! If you are a big fan it's worth reading but make sure that if you are purchasing it online as I did, that you don't pay too much since it's dinky!! </span>

<div id="review_415140333" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/415140333" />
    <a title="Gail Thompson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10777609-gail-thompson"><img alt="Gail Thompson" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/415140333?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gail Thompson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gail Thompson" href="/user/show/10777609-gail-thompson">Gail Thompson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10777609-gail-thompson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10777609-gail-thompson?shelf=fey">fey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10777609-gail-thompson?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10777609-gail-thompson?shelf=magic-users">magic-users</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10777609-gail-thompson?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer415140333" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4199477786544980401">This is a short book written for world book day and available to children for just a pound or free with a book token received from school. It is part of a set of books about the character of Artemis Fowl. Artemis is a boy whose father is missing. Nobody has been able to find him. Artemis cannot accept that his father is gone, and being highly intelligent, sets about finding his father by himself. He also wants to do something for his mother, who is devastated by the disappearance of his father, </span>
  <span id="freeText4199477786544980401" style="display:none">This is a short book written for world book day and available to children for just a pound or free with a book token received from school. It is part of a set of books about the character of Artemis Fowl. Artemis is a boy whose father is missing. Nobody has been able to find him. Artemis cannot accept that his father is gone, and being highly intelligent, sets about finding his father by himself. He also wants to do something for his mother, who is devastated by the disappearance of his father, “I will find him,” he whispered once in his mother’s arms. <br /><br />Finding out about the secret world of fairies, Artemis is convinced that this world can help him. There is just one problem, humans must not know about the fairy world. This world is different to our own, yet has a clear set of rules, and there are limits to the special abilities of those within it. This use of clear boundaries helps us to see it as more real, as if you could stumble across a secret world of fairies.<br /><br />This is a stand-alone story that also fits with the other books. The characters are well drawn, and the plot clear, so it is fine if you have not read any of the previous novels. Even though the story can be read independently, there are references to other tales, making the reader curious. Extra details about characters background and past actions help to give them further depth.<br /><br />There is also plenty of dialogue in the text, helping to keep the story fast paced. This is great for a children’s story as it keeps their attention throughout. The dialogue also helps to give further insight into the characters themselves, and to reveal details of the plot.<br /><br />There are often little placement lines written in italics at the start of a section of text. These quickly allow the reader to know exactly when and where they are. For instance, “police plaza. Haven City. The Lower Elements.” This is useful to younger readers who may find it harder to work out where they are or keep track. More cleverly, it enables the writer to keep the text shorter by omitting such information from the main body of the text, which would have to be written in a longer style. It also helps to break the text into manageable chunks, easier to cope with for young readers.<br /><br />I had not read any of the books about Artemis Fowl before, although I had certainly heard of them. They are clearly best selling children’s books for a reason. They are well written, have an original concept, and they are easy and entertaining to read. I hope to read more of these soon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4199477786544980401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17066508010463944118">This thriller adventure kept me on my toes from start to finish. The cover of the novel is just a hint onto what the book is about. This is the story of an adventure between a dwarf, Mulch, and Artemis Fowl, a 12-year-old criminal, in sight to steal the Fei Fei tiara. Artemis has a feeling that Mulch wants to steal the tiara too, and knows that to successfully steal it he will need Mulch’s help.   <span id="freeText17066508010463944118" style="display:none">This thriller adventure kept me on my toes from start to finish. The cover of the novel is just a hint onto what the book is about. This is the story of an adventure between a dwarf, Mulch, and Artemis Fowl, a 12-year-old criminal, in sight to steal the Fei Fei tiara. Artemis has a feeling that Mulch wants to steal the tiara too, and knows that to successfully steal it he will need Mulch’s help. The two make a plan to steal from Sergei and the Significants, who stole the tiara first, but come into some trouble when Holly the fairy tries to stop them. The ending is unexpected and exciting; the Epilogue is a must to read to know the real reason why Artemis Fowl wanted the blue stone of the tiara. This book would be a great for 3rd to 5th graders because it keeps you on your toes and anxious to know what happens next. The ending leaves a perfect segway to a series of novels, and keeps the readers reading what happens next! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14851367958466519000">The short novel "Artemis Fowl: The Seventh Dwarf" by Eion Colfer is one of the novels from the Artemis Foul series. The story focuses on a dwarf named Mulch Diggums who is after the Fei Fei tiara, but Artemis Fowl ( a 12 year old criminal) has other plans for him. This quick read is from a fantasy series and had quite the plot twist. Although i have never been drawn to the fantasy genre for novels, i enjoyed this short book. Reading it without knowing any background from the series was kind of d</span>
  <span id="freeText14851367958466519000" style="display:none">The short novel "Artemis Fowl: The Seventh Dwarf" by Eion Colfer is one of the novels from the Artemis Foul series. The story focuses on a dwarf named Mulch Diggums who is after the Fei Fei tiara, but Artemis Fowl ( a 12 year old criminal) has other plans for him. This quick read is from a fantasy series and had quite the plot twist. Although i have never been drawn to the fantasy genre for novels, i enjoyed this short book. Reading it without knowing any background from the series was kind of difficult but got easier to understand the further i got in the book. I think students would enjoy this book because the length is not overwhelming and it is without any pictures which would force children to use their imagination more. The cover of the novel alludes to an element in the story that is important to Artemis which is the blue diamond off of the notorious tiara. I would use this for students ages 9-12 and allow it to be more of a solo read than a class read. </span>

  <span id="freeText3308475300329166190" style="display:none"> In this book, Artemis has discovered that the time spell cast over Hybras is beginning to go bad and that demons will soon be thrown through time to certain death. <span id="freeTextContainer10030304249560218080">This is a World Book Day book, containing a single short story of about 60 pages in length. The story primarily feature Mulch Diggums but Artemis and Holly are involved. It's a pleasant enough amusing diversion but offers nothing that the Artemis Fowl novels don't. Since you won't find it except second hand or via an internet search I would suggest it is for die-hard Fowl fans only.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JCNOlzgWl8XWDey6ZbdogfIo1Vl450kxmiljfL1bU8/wuUmtviB4l1wNFl1eok7r6JHF4krSSAGCwmXuJa1tRA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer16977245802867561156">Eoin Colfer (pronounced Owen) was born in Wexford on the South-East coast of Ireland in 1965, where he and his four brothers were brought up by his father and mother, who were both educators.<br/><br/>He received his degree from Dublin University and began teaching primary school in Wexford. He has lived and worked all over the world, including Saudi Arabia, Tunisia and Italy. After the publication of the A</span>
  <span id="freeText16977245802867561156" style="display:none">Eoin Colfer (pronounced Owen) was born in Wexford on the South-East coast of Ireland in 1965, where he and his four brothers were brought up by his father and mother, who were both educators.<br /><br />He received his degree from Dublin University and began teaching primary school in Wexford. He has lived and worked all over the world, including Saudi Arabia, Tunisia and Italy. After the publication of the Artemis Fowl novels, Eoin retired from teaching and now writes full time. He lives in Ireland with his wife and two children.<br /><br /></span>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
